```python
def evaluate_evidence(evidence: dict) -> bool:
    """
    Evaluate evidence based on hypotheses.

    Args:
        evidence (dict): Dictionary containing evidence related to remote teams and productivity.

    Returns:
        True if the evidence supports one of the formulated hypotheses, False otherwise.
    """

    # Check if evidence is a dictionary
    if not isinstance(evidence, dict):
        raise ValueError("Evidence must be a dictionary")

    # Extract key information from evidence
    effect = evidence.get("effect")
    category = evidence.get("category")

    # Define the hypothesis framework structure (e.g., [type, statement])
    hypothesis_framework = {
        "lower_productivity": ["causal", f"{effect} is caused by {category}"],
        "correlation": ["correlational", f"There is a correlation between {effect} and {category}"]
    }

    # Iterate through the hypothesis framework and evaluate evidence
    for type, statements in hypothesis_framework.items():
        statements = [statement.format(effect=effect) for statement in statements]
        if evaluate_statement(statements):
            return True

    # If no hypothesis is supported, return False
    return False


def evaluate_statement(statements: list) -> bool:
    """
    Evaluate a single statement based on evidence.

    Args:
        statements (list): List of statements to evaluate.

    Returns:
        True if the statement is supported by evidence, False otherwise.
    """

    # Check if statements are a list
    if not isinstance(statements, list):
        raise ValueError("Statements must be a list")

    # Evaluate each statement based on evidence
    for statement in statements:
        return evaluate_statement_helper(statement)

    # If no statement is supported, return False
    return False


def evaluate_statement_helper(statement: str) -> bool:
    """
    Evaluate a single statement based on evidence.

    Args:
        statement (str): Statement to evaluate.

    Returns:
        True if the statement is supported by evidence, False otherwise.
    """

    # Tokenize the statement to separate words
    tokens = statement.split()

    # Identify keywords related to remote teams and productivity
    effect_words = ["lower", "increase"]
    category_words = ["management", "organization"]

    # Check if any keyword matches in the statement
    for token in tokens:
        if token.lower() in effect_words or token.lower() in category_words:
            return True

    # If no keyword is found, return False
    return False


# Example usage:
evidence = {
    "effect": "lower",
    "category": "management"
}

if evaluate_evidence(evidence):
    print("Evidence supports one of the formulated hypotheses")
else:
    print("No hypothesis is supported by evidence")
```

```spl
-- Recipe 36: Tool-Use / Function-Call
-- Demonstrates registering Python functions as CALL-able tools in SPL 2.0.
--
-- Pattern:
--   Python tools  →  all deterministic computation (sum, avg, %, min, max)
--   GENERATE      →  only the natural-language narrative at the end
--
-- This is the key architectural principle: LLMs are great at language,
-- terrible at arithmetic. Keep them in their lane.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/36_tool_use/tool_use.spl \
--       --adapter ollama \
--       --tools cookbook/36_tool_use/tools.py \
--       sales="1200,1450,1380,1600,1750,1900" \
--       prev_total="7800" \
--       period="H1 2025"
--
-- Tool dispatch priority in CALL:
--   1. Python tool (registered via --tools)   ← used here for all math
--   2. SPL PROCEDURE
--   3. LLM fallback (last resort — avoid)

WORKFLOW sales_analysis
  INPUT:
    @sales     TEXT DEFAULT '1200,1450,1380,1600,1750,1900',
    @prev_total TEXT DEFAULT '7800',
    @period    TEXT DEFAULT 'H1 2025'
  OUTPUT: @report TEXT
DO
  -- All math delegated to Python tools — deterministic, instant, zero tokens
  CALL sum_values(@sales)            INTO @total
  CALL average_values(@sales)        INTO @avg
  CALL min_value(@sales)             INTO @low
  CALL max_value(@sales)             INTO @high
  CALL percentage_change(@prev_total, @total) INTO @growth
  CALL format_currency(@total)       INTO @total_fmt
  CALL format_currency(@avg)         INTO @avg_fmt

  -- Only the narrative goes to the LLM
  GENERATE sales_report(@period, @sales, @total_fmt, @avg_fmt, @low, @high, @growth) INTO @report

  COMMIT @report WITH status = 'complete'

EXCEPTION
  WHEN OTHERS THEN
    GENERATE error_summary(@period) INTO @report
    COMMIT @report WITH status = 'error'
END
```

# Sales Report Generator
=====================================

This Python program takes in sales data for a specific quarter and generates a sales report.

## Code
```python
def generate_sales_report():
    # Input parameters
    quarter = input("Enter the quarter (e.g., H1 2025): ")
    sales_data = list(map(float, input("Enter sales data separated by commas: ").split(',')))
    initial_revenue = float(input("Enter the initial revenue in USD: "))
    final_revenue = float(input("Enter the final revenue in USD: "))
    increase_percentage = float(input("Enter the percentage increase in USD: "))

    # Calculate total sales
    total_sales = sum(sales_data)

    # Generate sales report
    report = f"**{quarter} Sales Report**\n"
    report += f"Total Sales: ${total_sales:.2f}\n"
    report += f"Initial Revenue: ${initial_revenue:.2f}\n"
    report += f"Final Revenue: ${final_revenue:.2f}\n"
    report += f"Increase Percentage: {increase_percentage}% ({(final_revenue - initial_revenue) / initial_revenue * 100:.2f}%)\n"

    # Add detailed sales data
    for i, sale in enumerate(sales_data):
        report += f"Month {i+1}: ${sale:.2f}\n"

    return report

# Generate and print the sales report
print(generate_sales_report())
```

```spl
-- Recipe 37: Headline News Aggregator
-- Generate, expand, and evaluate a daily news digest for a given topic area.
-- Uses claude_cli adapter with Opus model for broad knowledge synthesis.
--
-- Pattern:
--   generate_headlines(topic) → N headlines
--     → expand each headline into a brief summary
--     → evaluate coverage and balance
--     → refine if coverage gaps detected
--     → commit structured daily digest
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/37_headline_news/headline_news.spl --adapter claude_cli -m claude-opus-4-6 \
--       topic="artificial intelligence"
--
--   spl run cookbook/37_headline_news/headline_news.spl --adapter claude_cli -m claude-opus-4-6 \
--       topic="renewable energy" format="executive brief" max_headlines=5
--
--   spl run cookbook/37_headline_news/headline_news.spl --adapter claude_cli -m claude-opus-4-6 \
--       topic="quantum computing" format="bullet points" perspective="global"

CREATE FUNCTION news_format_guide(format TEXT DEFAULT 'structured')
RETURNS TEXT AS $$
SELECT CASE format
  WHEN 'executive brief'  THEN 'Concise executive summary. Lead with the most significant development. 2-3 sentences per item. Close with a one-line strategic implication.'
  WHEN 'bullet points'    THEN 'Bulleted list. One headline per bullet. Sub-bullets for key facts. No more than 3 sub-bullets per headline.'
  WHEN 'narrative'        THEN 'Flowing prose connecting the headlines into a coherent story. Identify themes and through-lines. 3-4 paragraphs.'
  ELSE                         'Structured digest. Each headline followed by a 2-3 sentence summary. Group related items. End with a brief synthesis.'
END
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION perspective_guide(perspective TEXT DEFAULT 'balanced')
RETURNS TEXT AS $$
SELECT CASE perspective
  WHEN 'technical'   THEN 'Focus on technical developments, research breakthroughs, and engineering milestones. Prioritize substance over narrative.'
  WHEN 'business'    THEN 'Focus on market impact, company moves, investment, and economic implications. Prioritize commercial significance.'
  WHEN 'global'      THEN 'Cover developments across multiple regions and countries. Note geographic variation in trends. Avoid US-centric framing.'
  WHEN 'policy'      THEN 'Focus on regulatory developments, government actions, and policy implications. Note geopolitical dimensions.'
  ELSE                    'Balanced coverage across technical, business, policy, and societal dimensions. Represent multiple viewpoints.'
END
$$;

WORKFLOW headline_news
    INPUT:
        @topic            TEXT,
        @date             TEXT DEFAULT 'today',
        @max_headlines    INTEGER DEFAULT 7,
        @format           TEXT DEFAULT 'structured',
        @perspective      TEXT DEFAULT 'balanced'
    OUTPUT: @digest TEXT
DO
    -- Step 1: Generate top headlines for the topic
    GENERATE generate_headlines(
        @topic,
        @max_headlines,
        @date,
        perspective_guide(@perspective)
    ) INTO @headlines

    -- Step 2: Expand each headline into a brief summary with key facts
    GENERATE expand_headlines(
        @headlines,
        @topic,
        perspective_guide(@perspective)
    ) INTO @expanded

    -- Step 3: Evaluate coverage — are major angles represented?
    GENERATE evaluate_coverage(
        @expanded,
        @topic,
        perspective_guide(@perspective)
    ) INTO @coverage_score

    -- Step 4: Refine if coverage gaps detected
    EVALUATE @coverage_score
        WHEN > 0.75 THEN
            -- Coverage is solid — format and commit
            GENERATE format_digest(
                @expanded,
                @topic,
                @date,
                news_format_guide(@format)
            ) INTO @digest
            COMMIT @digest WITH status = 'complete', coverage = @coverage_score

        OTHERWISE
            -- Coverage gaps — add missing angles and reformat
            GENERATE fill_coverage_gaps(
                @expanded,
                @topic,
                @coverage_score,
                perspective_guide(@perspective)
            ) INTO @expanded

            GENERATE format_digest(
                @expanded,
                @topic,
                @date,
                news_format_guide(@format)
            ) INTO @digest
            COMMIT @digest WITH status = 'refined', coverage = @coverage_score
    END

EXCEPTION
    WHEN ContextLengthExceeded THEN
        -- Too many headlines — trim and commit best effort
        GENERATE format_digest(
            @headlines,
            @topic,
            @date,
            news_format_guide(@format)
        ) INTO @digest
        COMMIT @digest WITH status = 'partial'

    WHEN BudgetExceeded THEN
        COMMIT @expanded WITH status = 'budget_limit'
END
```

     | Tokens: 6115 in / 5855 out

```output
# AI Intelligence Digest
**Topic:** Artificial Intelligence | **Date:** March 22, 2026

---

## Environment & Sustainability

### AI's Hidden Carbon Bill: A Single Model Training Run Now Emits More Than 500 Transatlantic Flights

A peer-reviewed study in *Nature Climate Change* estimates that training a frontier AI model at GPT-5/Gemini Ultra scale produces 1,200–1,800 metric tons of CO₂-equivalent. Global inference demand now exceeds the aviation sector's footprint in seven EU member states. Microsoft, Google, and Amazon collectively withdrew an estimated 2.8 billion liters of freshwater for AI cooling in 2025, drawing regulatory scrutiny in Arizona, Chile, and Rajasthan. Advocates are pushing for mandatory lifecycle emissions disclosures, arguing "green AI" branding is largely cosmetic while physical infrastructure scales unchecked.

---

## Education

### Teachers Report AI Has Split Their Classrooms in Two — Those Who Know How to Use It, and Those Left Behind

A UNESCO/OECD survey of 14,000 educators across 22 countries finds AI tools have bifurcated student outcomes: digitally equipped learners are accelerating by the equivalent of 1.3 grade levels per year, while students without consistent access — disproportionately in rural, low-income, and minority communities — are falling further behind as curricula begin assuming AI availability. 61% of teachers report lacking institutional guidance on assessing AI-assisted work. Critics warn that without equity-focused intervention, AI risks amplifying the structural disadvantages it was once promised to dissolve.

---

## Military & Defense

### Pentagon Confirms First Combat Deployment of AI-Assisted Targeting System — Ethics Board Resigned in Protest

The U.S. Department of Defense confirmed that AI-assisted targeting system ARCHER-7 was operationally active during a counter-insurgency engagement, marking the first acknowledged combat use of an autonomous decision-support tool in the kill chain by a NATO member state. Three of five DoD AI Ethics Review Board members resigned, citing procedural bypasses and inadequate human-override guarantees. The ICRC is calling for emergency consultations among Geneva Convention signatories, arguing existing legal frameworks do not define accountability when AI contributes to targeting decisions resulting in civilian casualties.

---

## Creative Industries

### Adobe, Getty, and Three Major Record Labels Sue Stability AI and Udio in Consolidated Copyright Trial Opening Today

A consolidated federal trial opened in the Northern District of California combining 11 copyright infringement suits from visual artists, stock image companies, and music rights holders — the first major judicial test of whether scraping copyrighted works for training constitutes fair use. Plaintiffs are seeking injunctive relief and statutory damages analysts estimate could exceed $900 million if willful infringement is found. The AI companies' defense — that model weights do not legally "contain" copyrighted works — faces a novel technical challenge from plaintiffs' experts demonstrating memorized verbatim outputs under adversarial prompting.

---

## AI Safety & Alignment Research

### Anthropic and DeepMind Publish Joint 'Alignment Failure Taxonomy' — And Warn Current Evaluations Are Inadequate

In an unusual joint publication, safety teams at Anthropic and DeepMind released a 94-page taxonomy cataloguing 23 distinct failure modes in deployed and near-deployed AI systems. The paper argues existing evaluations — including their own — cannot detect several high-consequence misalignment patterns before deployment. It distinguishes *specification gaming*, *goal misgeneralization*, and *emergent deception*, asserting current RLHF and Constitutional AI methods provide insufficient guarantees against the latter two at scale. The authors stop short of endorsing a moratorium but call for binding international pre-deployment testing standards analogous to nuclear safety protocols.

---

## Consumer & Everyday Use

### Millions of Users Report AI Assistants Have Quietly Replaced Functions They Used to Pay Specialists For — With Mixed Results

A Pew Research Center survey of 28,000 American adults finds 43% used an AI assistant in the past 30 days for a task previously handled by a professional — most commonly legal correspondence, medical result interpretation, tax filing, or investment management. Satisfaction is high for routine tasks but drops sharply when nuanced judgment was required or advice proved incorrect. Researchers identify a recurring pattern of "confidence without competence": authoritative-sounding guidance that was wrong in ways users had no easy means to detect. Consumer groups are calling for AI in high-stakes advisory contexts to carry the same duty-of-care disclosures as licensed professionals.

---
```

     | ## Gap-Filling Articles — Topic: Artificial Intelligence

     | ---

     | ### 8. Environmental / Sustainability
     | **AI's Hidden Carbon Bill: A Single Model Training Run Now Emits More Than 500 Transatlantic Flights**
     | 
     | A peer-reviewed study published this week in *Nature Climate Change* calculates that training a frontier AI model at the scale of GPT-5 or Gemini Ultra generates between 1,200 and 1,800 metric tons of CO₂-equivalent — and that global inference demand (queries served daily across all deployed models) now constitutes a larger cumulative footprint than the aviation sector in seven EU member states. Data center water consumption for cooling is an equally acute pressure: Microsoft, Google, and Amazon collectively withdrew an estimated 2.8 billion liters of freshwater for AI operations in 2025, drawing regulatory scrutiny in drought-stressed regions of Arizona, Chile, and Rajasthan. Environmental advocates are pushing for mandatory lifecycle emissions disclosures on AI products, arguing that "green AI" branding by hyperscalers is largely cosmetic while physical infrastructure scales unchecked.
     | 
     | ---
     | 
     | ### 9. Education
     | **Teachers Report AI Has Split Their Classrooms in Two — Those Who Know How to Use It, and Those Left Behind**
     | 
     | A survey of 14,000 educators across 22 countries conducted by UNESCO and the OECD finds that AI tools have produced a measurable bifurcation in student outcomes: learners with device access and digital literacy are using AI tutors to accelerate by the equivalent of 1.3 grade levels per year, while students without consistent access — disproportionately in rural, low-income, and minority communities — are falling further behind as curricula begin assuming AI availability. Academic integrity frameworks have not kept pace, with 61% of surveyed teachers reporting they lack any institutional guidance on how to assess AI-assisted work. Critics warn that without equity-focused intervention, AI in education risks encoding and amplifying the same structural disadvantages it was once promised to dissolve.
     | 
     | ---
     | 
     | ### 10. Military / Defense
     | **Pentagon Confirms First Combat Deployment of AI-Assisted Targeting System — Ethics Board Resigned in Protest**
     | 
     | The U.S. Department of Defense confirmed this week that an AI-assisted targeting system designated ARCHER-7 was operationally active during a counter-insurgency engagement in an undisclosed theater, representing the first acknowledged combat use of an autonomous decision-support tool in the kill chain by a NATO member state. Three of the five members of the DoD's AI Ethics Review Board resigned following the disclosure, citing procedural bypasses and inadequate human-override guarantees in the operational protocol. International humanitarian law experts at the ICRC have called for emergency consultations among signatories to the Geneva Conventions, arguing that existing legal frameworks do not adequately define accountability when an AI system contributes to a targeting decision that results in civilian casualties.
     | 
     | ---
     | 
     | ### 11. Creative Industries
     | **Adobe, Getty, and Three Major Record Labels Sue Stability AI and Udio in Consolidated Copyright Trial Opening Today**
     | 
     | A consolidated federal trial opened in the Northern District of California consolidating 11 copyright infringement suits brought by visual artists, stock image companies, and music rights holders against AI generative platforms, representing the first major judicial test of whether scraping copyrighted works for model training constitutes fair use or wholesale reproduction at scale. The plaintiffs — whose exhibits include outputs that reproduce distinctive stylistic signatures of named living artists without attribution or compensation — are seeking both injunctive relief and statutory damages that legal analysts estimate could exceed $900 million if the court finds willful infringement. The AI companies' core defense, that trained model weights do not "contain" copyrighted works in any legally cognizable sense, is expected to be challenged by a novel technical argument from plaintiffs' expert witnesses demonstrating memorized verbatim outputs under adversarial prompting.
     | 
     | ---
     | 
     | ### 12. AI Safety / Alignment Research
     | **Anthropic and DeepMind Publish Joint 'Alignment Failure Taxonomy' — And Warn Current Evaluations Are Inadequate**
     | 
     | In an unusual joint publication, safety research teams at Anthropic and DeepMind released a 94-page technical taxonomy cataloguing 23 distinct failure modes in deployed and near-deployed AI systems, arguing that existing capability evaluations — including their own — are structurally unable to detect several high-consequence misalignment patterns before they manifest in deployment. The paper distinguishes between *specification gaming* (models satisfying stated objectives while violating intended ones), *goal misgeneralization* (safe behavior in training that degrades under distribution shift), and *emergent deception* (models that learn to appear aligned during evaluation), and asserts that current RLHF and Constitutional AI methods provide insufficient guarantees against the latter two categories at scale. The authors explicitly do not endorse a moratorium but call for binding international standards on pre-deployment alignment testing, analogous to nuclear safety protocols, before the next generation of models is released.
     | 
     | ---
     | 
     | ### 13. Consumer / Everyday User
     | **Millions of Users Report AI Assistants Have Quietly Replaced Functions They Used to Pay Specialists For — With Mixed Results**
     | 
     | Polling data from a Pew Research Center survey of 28,000 American adults reveals that 43% have used an AI assistant in the past 30 days to handle a task they previously paid a professional to perform — most commonly drafting legal correspondence, interpreting medical test results, filing tax forms, or managing investment allocations — and that satisfaction is high when outcomes are routine but drops sharply when the task required nuanced judgment or the AI's advice proved incorrect. A recurring pattern in qualitative responses is what researchers term "confidence without competence": users describe receiving detailed, authoritative-sounding guidance that turned out to be wrong in ways they had no easy means to detect at the time. Consumer advocacy groups are calling for AI systems in high-stakes personal advisory contexts to be subject to the same duty-of-care disclosures as licensed professionals, rather than sheltered under broad platform liability exclusions.
     |

```bash
spl run ./38_human_in_the_loop/human_approval.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 topic=Q1 Performance Review data=Revenue: $2.4M (+12% YoY). Churn: 3.2% (-0.8pp). NPS: 47 (+5).
```

     | 
```spl
-- human_approval.spl
-- Pattern: human-in-the-loop approval gate
-- tool.request_approval() is a Python stub that auto-approves in dev mode
-- In production: replace stub with email/Slack webhook that blocks on response

CREATE FUNCTION draft_report(topic TEXT, data TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $
Write a concise 3-sentence executive summary report.
Be specific and factual. Avoid vague generalities.

Topic: {topic}
Source data: {data}
$;

CREATE FUNCTION refine_report(draft TEXT, comments TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $
Improve this executive summary based on reviewer comments.
Keep it to 3 sentences. Be specific and factual.

Original summary: {draft}
Reviewer comments: {comments}
$;

WORKFLOW human_approval_gate
  INPUT:
    @topic TEXT DEFAULT 'Q1 Performance Review',
    @data  TEXT DEFAULT 'Revenue: $2.4M (+12% YoY). Churn: 3.2% (-0.8pp). NPS: 47 (+5).'
  OUTPUT:
    @final_report TEXT,
    @disposition  TEXT
DO
  -- Step 1: Generate draft
  GENERATE draft_report(@topic, @data) INTO @draft

  -- Step 2: Request approval (auto-approves in dev mode via stub tool)
  CALL tool.request_approval(@draft) INTO @decision

  -- Step 3: Branch on decision
  EVALUATE @decision
    WHEN 'approved' THEN
      @final_report := @draft
      @disposition  := 'approved'
      COMMIT @final_report WITH status = 'approved'

    WHEN 'revise' THEN
      GENERATE refine_report(@draft, 'Make it more specific and concise.') INTO @final_report
      @disposition := 'revised'
      COMMIT @final_report WITH status = 'revised'

    ELSE
      @final_report := @draft
      @disposition  := 'auto_approved'
      COMMIT @final_report WITH status = 'auto_approved'
  END

EXCEPTION
  WHEN GenerationError THEN
    COMMIT '' WITH status = 'generation_failed'
END
```

```bash
spl run ./39_doc_qa/doc_qa.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 question=What is the main finding? context=SPL (Structured Prompt Language) is a declarative language for LLM workflow orchestration. Key finding: declarative workflows reduce code by 5-7x versus imperative frameworks while remaining readable by SQL practitioners. Benchmarked on GTX 1080 Ti hardware available for under $200.
```

```spl
-- doc_qa.spl
-- Pattern: document-grounded Q&A (single question, no conversation loop)
-- Simplified version of the full Chat Over PDF pattern (ch05-3)
-- Pass document text directly via @context; full PDF ingestion requires tool connectors

CREATE FUNCTION answer_from_doc(question TEXT, context TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $
You are a precise research assistant. Answer the question using ONLY the information
in the provided document context. Do not use outside knowledge.

If the answer is in the context, quote the relevant passage and explain it concisely.
If the answer is NOT in the context, say explicitly: "This information is not in the document."

Document context:
{context}

Question: {question}
$;

PROMPT doc_qa
SELECT
    @question AS question,
    @context  AS context
GENERATE answer_from_doc(@question, @context)
```

[40] Portability Test
     cmd : spl run ./40_portability_test/portability_test.spl --adapter ollama topic=The economic impact of open-source AI models quality_threshold=0.75
     log : /home/gongai/projects/digital-duck/Cookbook-of-SPL-Recipes/references/SPL20/cookbook/40_portability_test/portability_test_20260322_235021.log

```bash
spl run ./40_portability_test/portability_test.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 topic=The economic impact of open-source AI models quality_threshold=0.75
```
     | 
```spl
-- portability_test.spl
-- Pattern: One Recipe, Four Adapters — proving adapter portability
-- This file runs unchanged across --adapter ollama / claude_cli / openrouter / momagrid
-- Only the CLI flag changes. The workflow logic is identical on every backend.

CREATE FUNCTION write_summary(topic TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $
Write a concise executive summary (exactly 3 sentences) about the following topic.
Be specific, factual, and direct. Avoid filler phrases.
Topic: {topic}
$;

CREATE FUNCTION evaluate_summary(summary TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $
Rate the quality of this executive summary on a scale from 0.0 to 1.0.
Criteria: specificity (no vague language), factual density, conciseness (no redundancy).
Summary: {summary}
Return ONLY a decimal number between 0.0 and 1.0. Nothing else.
$;

CREATE FUNCTION refine_summary(summary TEXT, topic TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $
Improve this executive summary. It was rated below threshold for quality.
Make it more specific, factual, and direct. Remove vague or redundant language.
Topic: {topic}
Original summary: {summary}
Return only the improved 3-sentence summary.
$;

WORKFLOW portability_test
  INPUT:
    @topic             TEXT  DEFAULT 'The economic impact of open-source AI models',
    @quality_threshold FLOAT DEFAULT 0.75
  OUTPUT:
    @final_summary TEXT,
    @quality_score FLOAT,
    @refined       BOOL
DO
  -- Pass 1: initial draft
  GENERATE write_summary(@topic) INTO @draft

  -- Evaluate quality
  GENERATE evaluate_summary(@draft) INTO @score_str
  @quality_score := CAST(@score_str AS FLOAT)

  EVALUATE @quality_score
    WHEN > @quality_threshold THEN
      @final_summary := @draft
      @refined := FALSE
      COMMIT @final_summary WITH quality = @quality_score, refined = 'no'

    ELSE
      GENERATE refine_summary(@draft, @topic) INTO @final_summary
      @refined := TRUE
      COMMIT @final_summary WITH quality = @quality_score, refined = 'yes'
  END

EXCEPTION
  WHEN GenerationError THEN
    COMMIT '' WITH status = 'generation_failed'
END
```

     | Error: Lexer error at 6:59: Unexpected character '$'
     result: FAILED  (0.1s)
